   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    Voiced dental and alveolar stops
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

     </a>

     </a>

             <source data-bandwidth="108571" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file (109 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/01/Voiced_alveolar_plosive.ogg" type='audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"'/>

       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        voiced alveolar stop
       </b>
       is a type of
       <a href="/wiki/Consonant" title="Consonant">
        consonantal
       </a>
       sound, used in some
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Speech_communication" title="Speech communication">
        spoken
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">
        languages
       </a>
       . The symbol in the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
        International Phonetic Alphabet
       </a>
       that represents voiced
       <a href="/wiki/Dental_consonant" title="Dental consonant">
        dental
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_consonant" title="Alveolar consonant">
        alveolar
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Postalveolar_consonant" title="Postalveolar consonant">
        postalveolar
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Stop_consonant" title="Stop consonant">
        stops
       </a>
       is ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        d
       </span>
       ⟩ (although the symbol ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        d̪
       </span>
       ⟩ can be used to distinguish the dental stop, and ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        d̠
       </span>
       ⟩ the postalveolar), and the equivalent
       <a href="/wiki/X-SAMPA" title="X-SAMPA">
        X-SAMPA
       </a>
       symbol is
       <code>
        d
       </code>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Features">
        Features
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Voiced_dental_and_alveolar_stops&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Features">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Features of the voiced alveolar stop:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Manner_of_articulation" title="Manner of articulation">
         manner of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Occlusive" title="Occlusive">
         occlusive
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by obstructing airflow in the vocal tract. Since the consonant is also oral, with no
        <a href="/wiki/Nasal_consonant" title="Nasal consonant">
         nasal outlet
        </a>
        , the airflow is blocked entirely, and the consonant is a
        <a href="/wiki/Stop_consonant" title="Stop consonant">
         stop
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        There are three specific variants of
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [d]
        </span>
        :
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Dental_consonant" title="Dental consonant">
           Dental
          </a>
          , which means it is articulated with either the tip or the blade of the tongue at the upper
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teeth" title="Teeth">
           teeth
          </a>
          , termed respectively
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Apical_consonant" title="Apical consonant">
            apical
           </a>
          </i>
          and
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Laminal_consonant" title="Laminal consonant">
            laminal
           </a>
          </i>
          .
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Denti-alveolar_consonant" title="Denti-alveolar consonant">
           Denti-alveolar
          </a>
          , which means it is articulated with the blade of the tongue at the
          <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_ridge" title="Alveolar ridge">
           alveolar ridge
          </a>
          , and the tip of the tongue behind upper teeth.
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_consonant" title="Alveolar consonant">
           Alveolar
          </a>
          , which means it is articulated with either the tip or the blade of the tongue at the alveolar ridge, termed respectively
          <i>
           apical
          </i>
          and
          <i>
           laminal
          </i>
          .
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Phonation" title="Phonation">
         phonation
        </a>
        is voiced, which means the vocal cords vibrate during the articulation.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is an
        <a href="/wiki/Oral_consonant" title="Oral consonant">
         oral consonant
        </a>
        , which means air is allowed to escape through the mouth only.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is a
        <a href="/wiki/Central_consonant" title="Central consonant">
         central consonant
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by directing the airstream along the center of the tongue, rather than to the sides.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Airstream_mechanism" title="Airstream mechanism">
         airstream mechanism
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Egressive_sound" title="Egressive sound">
         pulmonic
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated by pushing air solely with the
        <a href="/wiki/Lung" title="Lung">
         lungs
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Thoracic_diaphragm" title="Thoracic diaphragm">
         diaphragm
        </a>
        , as in most sounds.
       </li>
      </ul>

          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [diːn]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'religion'
        </td>
        <td>
         Laminal denti-alveolar or alveolar, depending on the dialect. See
         <a href="/wiki/Arabic_phonology" title="Arabic phonology">
          Arabic phonology
         </a>
         .
        </td>

         'roof'
        </td>

          [d̻ɑns]

        <td>
         'dance'
        </td>
        <td>
         Partially voiced or fully voiceless
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [
          <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_dental_and_alveolar_stops#Alveolar" title="Voiceless dental and alveolar stops">
           t
          </a>
          ]
         </span>
         . Varies between laminal denti-alveolar and laminal alveolar.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kris22_33-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-kris22-33">
           [33]
          </a>
         </sup>
         See
         <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_phonology" title="Norwegian phonology">
          Norwegian phonology
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>

         'office'
        </td>

            <i>
             <b>

             </b>

         <span class="nounderlines nowrap">
          <span class="unicode haudio">
           <span class="fn">
            <span style="white-space:nowrap">
             <a href="/wiki/File:SK-do.ogg" title="About this sound">
              <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
             </a>
            </span>
            <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/60/SK-do.ogg" title="SK-do.ogg">
             <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
              [d̻o̞]
             </span>
            </a>
           </span>
           <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
            (
            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
             <span style="cursor:help;">
              help
             </span>
            </a>
            ·
            <a href="/wiki/File:SK-do.ogg" title="File:SK-do.ogg">
             <span style="cursor:help;">
              info
             </span>
            </a>
            )
           </small>
          </span>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'into'
        </td>
        <td>
         Varies between laminal denti-alveolar and laminal alveolar.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKráľ198872_35-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKráľ198872-35">
           [35]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPavlík200498–99_36-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPavlík200498–99-36">
           [36]
          </a>
         </sup>
         See
         <a href="/wiki/Slovak_phonology" title="Slovak phonology">
          Slovak phonology
         </a>
        </td>

        <td>

          Swedish
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         Central Standard
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-riad46_37-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-riad46-37">
           [37]

         <i>
          <span lang="sv">
           <a href="/wiki/Swedish_alphabet" title="Swedish alphabet">
            <i>
             <b>
              d
             </b>
             ag
            </i>
           </a>
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [dɑːɡ]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'day'
        </td>
        <td>
         Varies between laminal denti-alveolar and alveolar, with the former being predominant.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-riad46_37-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-riad46-37">
           [37]
          </a>
         </sup>
         May be an
         <a href="/wiki/Voiced_dental_fricative" title="Voiced dental fricative">
          approximant
         </a>
         in casual speech. See
         <a href="/wiki/Swedish_phonology" title="Swedish phonology">
          Swedish phonology
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>

                         voiceless consonant
                        </a>
                        , and the rightmost represents a
                        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_consonant" title="Voiced consonant">
                         voiced consonant
                        </a>
                        .
                       </p>
                       <p>
                        Shaded areas denote articulations judged to be impossible.
                       </p>
                      </td>
                     </tr>
                    </table>
                   </div>
                  </td>
                 </tr>
                </table>
               </td>
              </tr>
